In summary, the game unfolded with a sense of distrust and shifting suspicions among players. Initially, player 0 voted for player 3, citing concerns about appearing irrational or werewolf-aligned if he voted against player 2. He justified targeting player 3 due to the strong accusations from player 1, believed to be the seer, who also voted for player 3 with the intention of exposing an alliance between players 0 and 3.

Player 2, on the other hand, went against player 3 as well, fearing that voting for player 0 would diminish his standing with the villagers since player 3 was already under heavy suspicion. Player 3 retaliated by voting for player 1, trying to suggest player 6 was suspicious, possibly to divert attention from themselves. Player 4 supported this move, targeting player 1 as part of a werewolf strategy to create confusion and avoid detection.

Player 6, caught in the crossfire, chose to vote against player 3, hoping to align with the perception of player 1 as a trusted seer. However, in a turbulent turn of events, player 6 found himself voted out and was eliminated. The night phase saw the demise of player 2, and

Reflecting on the previous game, it appears that some of my expectations did align with my imagination, particularly my prediction about increased scrutiny of player 6's behavior after my speech. However, the outcome that player 6 was voted out suggests that I may have underestimated the persuasive power of direct accusation, even without concrete evidence. The fact that player 6 was eliminated after my speech implies that the other players may have been more easily swayed by suspicion than anticipated.

What I did not expect was the aggressive reactions that ensued, especially player 3 voting against player 1, possibly in an attempt to steer suspicion away from themselves. Additionally, the strategic voting patterns of players 4 and 6, as well as the nighttime elimination of player 2, were unforeseen developments that hint at the need to adapt my evaluation of voting patterns accoordingly.

Considering my action proposals, I'm wondering if placing a stronger emphasis on concrete evidence rather than confronting a specific player could have been a superior approach.
